20">ISEQ 20</a></td>\n<td>ISEQ20</td>\n<td>EUR\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal"><img alt="Portugal" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Portugal.svg/23px-Flag_of_Portugal.svg.png" decoding="async" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Portugal.svg/35px-Flag_of_Portugal.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Portugal.svg/45px-Flag_of_Portugal.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="400" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/PSI-20" title="PSI-20">PSI 20</a></td>\n<td>PSI20</td>\n<td>EUR\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway"><img alt="Norway" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Flag_of_Norway.svg/21px-Flag_of_Norway.svg.png" decoding="async" width="21" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Flag_of_Norway.svg/32px-Flag_of_Norway.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Flag_of_Norway.svg/41px-Flag_of_Norway.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="372" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/OBX_Index" title="OBX Index">OBX 25</a></td>\n<td>OBX</td>\n<td>NOK\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_securities_depository">Central securities depository</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euronext&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Central securities depository">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Euronext provides custody and settlement services through <a href="/wiki/Central_securities_depository" title="Central securities depository">central securities depositaries</a> (CSD) in Denmark, Norway and Portugal.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_exhange_trading">Foreign exhange trading</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euronext&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Foreign exhange trading">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><i>Euronext FX</i> is a global <a href="/wiki/Foreign_exchange_trading" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign exchange trading">foreign exchange trading</a> platform, known as <i>FastMatch</i> until 2019.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euronext&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Other">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Euronext operates regulated equity and <a href="/wiki/Derivative_(finance)" title="Derivative (finance)">derivatives</a> markets and is the largest centre for debt and funds listings in the world. Its product range includes <a href="/wiki/Equities" class="mw-redirect" title="Equities">equities</a>, <a href="/wiki/Exchange-traded_fund" title="Exchange-traded fund">exchange-traded funds</a>, warrants and certificates, <a href="/wiki/Bond_(finance)" title="Bond (finance)">bonds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Derivative_(finance)" title="Derivative (finance)">derivatives</a> and <a href="/wiki/Commodities" class="mw-redirect" title="Commodities">commodities</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_information">Financial information</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euronext&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Financial information">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align: center">\n<caption>(amounts in millions)\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th width="50pt">Year<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</th>\n<th width="80pt">Revenue\n</th>\n<th width="80pt"><a href="/wiki/EBITDA" class="mw-redirect" title="EBITDA">EBITDA</a>\n</th>\n<th width="80pt">Net result\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2014</td>\n<td>\xe2\x82\xac458,5</td>\n<td>\xe2\x82\xac225,4</td>\n<td>\xe2\x82\xac118,2\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2015</td>\n<td>\xe2\x82\xac518,5</td>\n<td>\xe2\x82\xac283,8</td>\n<td>\xe2\x82\xac172,7\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2016</td>\n<td>\xe2\x82\xac496,4</td>\n<td>\xe2\x82\xac283,9</td>\n<td>\xe2\x82\xac197,0\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2017</td>\n<td>\xe2\x82\xac532,3</td>\n<td>\xe2\x82\xac297,8</td>\n<td>\xe2\x82\xac241,3\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2018</td>\n<td>\xe2\x82\xac615,0</td>\n<td>\xe2\x82\xac354,3</td>\n<td>\xe2\x82\xac216,0\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2019</td>\n<td>\xe2\x82\xac679,1</td>\n<td>\xe2\x82\xac399,4</td>\n<td>\xe2\x82\xac222,0\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>2020</td>\n<td>\xe2\x82\xac884,3</td>\n<td>\xe2\x82\xac520,0</td>\n<td>\xe2\x82\xac315,5\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euronext&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Background:_Pre-merger_bourses">Background: Pre-merger bourses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euronext&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Background: Pre-merger bourses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span id="Amsterdam_.281602.E2.80.932000.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Amsterdam_(1602\xe2\x80\x932000)">Amsterdam (1602\xe2\x80\x932000)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euronext&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Amsterdam (1602\xe2\x80\x932000)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vereinigte_Ostindische_Compagnie_bond_-_Middelburg_-_Amsterdam_-_1622.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Vereinigte_Ostindische_Compagnie_bond_-_Middelburg_-_Amsterdam_-_1622.jpg/220px-Vereinigte_Ostindische_Compagnie_bond_-_Middelburg_-_Amsterdam_-_1622.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="182" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Vereinigte_Ostindische_Compagnie_bond_-_Middelburg_-_Amsterdam_-_1622.jpg/330px-Vereinigte_Ostindische_Compagnie_bond_-_Middelburg_-_Amsterdam_-_1622.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Vereinigte_Ostindische_Compagnie_bond_-_Middelburg_-_Amsterdam_-_1622.jpg/440px-Vereinigte_Ostindische_Compagnie_bond_-_Middelburg_-_Amsterdam_-_1622.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="528" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vereinigte_Ostindische_Compagnie_bond_-_Middelburg_-_Amsterdam_-_1622.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Bond_(finance)" title="Bond (finance)">bond</a> from the Dutch East India Company, dating from 7&#160;November 1623, for the amount of 2,400 <a href="/wiki/Dutch_guilder" title="Dutch guilder">florins</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Amsterdam Stock Exchange (<a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <i lang="nl">Amsterdamse effectenbeurs</i>) was considered the oldest "modern" securities market in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Braudel_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Braudel-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> It was shortly after the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">Dutch East India Company</a> (VOC) in 1602 when equities began trading on a regular basis as a secondary market to trade its shares. Prior to that, the market existed primarily for the exchange of commodities.<sup id="cite_ref-Stringham_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stringham-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> In that year, the <a href="/wiki/States_General_of_the_Netherlands" title="States General of the Netherlands">States General of the Netherlands</a> granted the VOC a 21-year charter over all Dutch trade in Asia and quasi-governmental powers. The monopolistic terms of the charter effectively granted the VOC complete authority over trade defenses, war armaments, and political endeavors in Asia. The first multi-national corporation with significant resource interests was thereby established. In addition, the high level of risk associated with trade in Asia gave the VOC its private ownership structure. Following in the footsteps of the English East India Company, stock in the corporation was sold to a large pool of interested investors, who in turn received a guarantee of some future share of profits.<sup id="cite_ref-Vries_1815,_p._384_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vries_1815,_p._384-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In the Amsterdam East India House alone, 1,143 investors subscribed for over \xc6\x923,679,915 or \xe2\x82\xac100 million in today\'s money.<sup id="cite_ref-L.O._Petram._FGw_2011._p._2_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-L.O._Petram._FGw_2011._p._2-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AMH-4803-KB_The_city_hall_on_Batavia.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/AMH-4803-KB_The_city_hall_on_Batavia.jpg/220px-AMH-4803-KB_The_city_hall_on_Batavia.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/AMH-4803-KB_The_city_hall_on_Batavia.jpg/330px-AMH-4803-KB_The_city_hall_on_Batavia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/AMH-4803-KB_The_city_hall_on_Batavia.jpg/440px-AMH-4803-KB_The_city_hall_on_Batavia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="1951" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AMH-4803-KB_The_city_hall_on_Batavia.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The city hall of <a href="/wiki/History_of_Jakarta" title="History of Jakarta">Batavia</a>, during the Dutch East Indies period.</div></div></div>\n<p>The subscription terms of each stock purchase offered shareholders the option to transfer their shares to a third party. Quickly a secondary market arose in the East India House for resale of this stock through the official bookkeeper. After an agreement had been reached between the two parties, the shares were then transferred from seller to buyer in the "capital book".<sup id="cite_ref-L.O._Petram._FGw_2011._p._2_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-L.O._Petram._FGw_2011._p._2-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> The official account, held by the East India House, encouraged investors to trade and gave rise to market confidence that the shares weren\'t just being transferred on paper.<sup id="cite_ref-L.O._Petram._FGw_2011._p._2_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-L.O._Petram._FGw_2011._p._2-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Thus, speculative trading immediately ensued and the Amsterdam securities market was born.\n</p><p>A big acceleration in the turnover rate came in 1623, after the 21-year liquidation period for the VOC ended. The terms of the initial charter called for a full liquidation after 21 years to distribute profits to shareholders. However, at this time neither the VOC nor its shareholders saw a slowing down of Asian trade, so the States General of the Netherlands granted the corporation a second charter in the West Indies.\n</p><p>This new charter gave the VOC additional years to stay in business but, in contrast to the first charter, outlined no plans for immediate liquidation, meaning that the money invested remained invested, and dividends were paid to investors to incentivize shareholding. Investors took to the secondary market of the newly constructed Amsterdam Stock Exchange to sell their shares to third parties.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> These "fixed" capital stock transactions amassed huge turnover rates, and made the stock exchange vastly more important. Thus the modern securities market arose out of this system of stock exchange.\n</p><p>The voyage to the precious resources in the West Indies was risky. Threats of pirates, disease, misfortune, shipwreck, and various macroeconomic factors heightened the risk factor and thus made the trip wildly expensive. So, the stock issuance made possible the spreading of risk and dividends across a vast pool of investors. Should something go wrong on the voyage, risk was mitigated and dispersed throughout the pool and investors all suffered just a fraction of the total expense of the voyage.\n</p><p>The system of privatizing national expeditions was not new to Europe, but the fixed stock structure of the East India Company made it one of a kind. In the decade preceding the formation of the VOC, adventurous Dutch merchants had used a similar method of "private partnership" to finance expensive voyages to the East Indies for their personal gain.<sup id="cite_ref-John_F._Padgett_2012._p._227_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-John_F._Padgett_2012._p._227-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The ambitious merchants pooled money together to create shipping partnerships for exploration of the East Indies. They assumed a joint-share of the necessary preparations (i.e. shipbuilding, stocking, navigation) in return for a joint-share of the profits.<sup id="cite_ref-John_F._Padgett_2012._p._227_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-John_F._Padgett_2012._p._227-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> These <i>Voorcompagnie\xc3\xabn</i> took on extreme risk to reap some of the rewarding spice trade in the East Indies, but introduced a common form of the joint-stock venture into Dutch shipping.\n</p><p>Although some of these voyages predictably failed, the ones that were successful brought promise of wealth and an emerging new trade. Shortly after these expeditions began, in 1602, the many independent <i>Voorcompagnie\xc3\xabn</i> merged to form the massive Dutch East India Trading Company.<sup id="cite_ref-John_F._Padgett_2012._p._227_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-John_F._Padgett_2012._p._227-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Shares were allocated appropriately by the Amsterdam Stock Exchange and the joint-stock merchants became the directors of the new VOC.<sup id="cite_ref-John_F._Padgett_2012._p._227_25-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-John_F._Padgett_2012._p._227-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Furthermore, this new mega-corporation was immediately recognized by the Dutch provinces to be equally important in governmental procedures. The VOC was granted significant war-time powers, the right to build forts, the right to maintain a standing army, and permission to conduct negotiations with Asian countries.<sup id="cite_ref-Vries_1815,_p._384_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vries_1815,_p._384-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> The charter created a Dutch colonial province in Indonesia, with a monopoly on Euro-Asian trade.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Job_Adriaensz._Berckheyde_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Job_Adriaensz._Berckheyde_001.jpg/220px-Job_Adriaensz._Berckheyde_001.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Job_Adriaensz._Berckheyde_001.jpg/330px-Job_Adriaensz._Berckheyde_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Job_Adriaensz._Berckheyde_001.jpg/440px-Job_Adriaensz._Berckheyde_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1261" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Job_Adriaensz._Berckheyde_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Courtyard of the Amsterdam Stock Exchange, circa 1670.</div></div></div>\n<p>The rapid development of the Amsterdam Stock exchange in the mid 17th century lead to the formation of trading clubs around the city. Traders met frequently, often in a local coffee shop or inns to discuss financial transactions. Thus, "Sub-markets" emerged, in which traders had access to peer knowledge and a community of reputable traders.\n</p><p>These were particularly important during trading in the late 17th century, where short-term speculative trading dominated. The trading clubs allowed investors to attain valuable information from reputable traders about the future of the securities trade.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> Experienced traders on the inside circle of these trading clubs had a slight advantage over everyone else, and the prevalence of these clubs played a major role in the continued growth of the stock exchange itself.\n</p><p>Additionally, similarities can be drawn between modern day brokers and the experienced traders of the trading clubs. The network of traders allowed for organized movement of knowledge and quick execution of transactions. Thus, the secondary market for VOC shares became extremely efficient, and trading clubs played no small part. Brokers took a small fee in exchange for a guarantee that the paperwork would be appropriately filed and a "buyer" or "seller" would be found. Throughout the 17th century, investors increasingly sought experienced brokers to seek information about a potential counterparty.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The European Options Exchange (EOE) was founded in 1978 in Amsterdam as a <a href="/wiki/Futures_contract" title="Futures contract">futures</a> and <a href="/wiki/Option_(finance)" title="Option (finance)">options</a> exchange. In 1983 it started a <a href="/wiki/Stock_market_index" title="Stock market index">stock market index</a>, called the EOE index, consisting of the 25 largest companies that trade on the stock exchange. <a href="/wiki/Forward_contract" title="Forward contract">Forward contracts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Option_(finance)" title="Option (finance)">options</a>, and other sophisticated instruments were traded on the Amsterdam Stock Exchange well before this.<sup id="cite_ref-Stringham_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stringham-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1997 the Amsterdam Stock Exchange and the EOE merged, and its blue chip index was renamed <a href="/wiki/AEX_index" title="AEX index">AEX</a>, for "Amsterdam EXchange". It is now managed by Euronext Amsterdam.\nOn 3 October 2011, <a href="/wiki/Princess_M%C3%A1xima" class="mw-redirect" title="Princess M\xc3\xa1xima">Princess M\xc3\xa1xima</a> opened the new trading floor of the Amsterdam Stock Exchange.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The former Stock Exchange building was the <a href="/wiki/Beurs_van_Berlage" title="Beurs van Berlage">Beurs van Berlage</a>.\n</p><p>Although it is usually considered to be the first stock market, <a href="/wiki/Fernand_Braudel" title="Fernand Braudel">Fernand Braudel</a> argues that this is not precisely true:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r996844942">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote">\n<p>"It is not quite accurate to call [Amsterdam] the first stock market, as people often do. State loan stocks had been negotiable at a very early date in Venice, in Florence before 1328, and in Genoa, where there was an active market in the luoghi and paghe of Casa di San Giorgio, not to mention the Kuxen shares in the German mines which were quoted as early as the fifteenth century at the Leipzig fairs, the Spanish juros, the French rentes sur l\xe2\x80\x99Hotel de Ville (municipal stocks) (1522) or the stock market in the Hanseatic towns from the fifteenth century. The statutes of Verona in 1318 confirm the existence of the settlement or forward market ... In 1428, the jurist Bartolomeo de Bosco protested against the sale of forward loca in Genoa. All evidence points to the Mediterranean as the cradle of the stock market. But what was new in Amsterdam was the volume, the fluidity of the market and publicity it received, and the speculative freedom of transactions."\n</p>\n<div class="templatequotecite">\xe2\x80\x94&#8201;<cite>Fernand Braudel (1983)<sup id="cite_ref-Braudel_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Braudel-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></cite></div></blockquote>\n<p>However, it is the first incarnation of what we could today recognize as a stock market.\n</p><p>The Amsterdam Bourse, an open-air venue, was created as a commodity exchange in 1530 and rebuilt in 1608.<sup id="cite_ref-De_la_Vega_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-De_la_Vega-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Rather than being a bazaar where goods were traded intermittently, exchanges had the advantage of being a regularly meeting market, which enabled traders to become more specialized and engage in more complicated transactions.<sup id="cite_ref-Braudel_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Braudel-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Stringham_21-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stringham-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> As early as the middle of the sixteenth century, people in Amsterdam speculated in grain and, somewhat later, in herring, spices, whale-oil, and even tulips. The Amsterdam Bourse in particular was the place where this kind of business was carried on. This institution as an open-air market in Warmoestreet, later moved for a while to the \xe2\x80\x98New Bridge,\xe2\x80\x99 which crosses the Damrak, then flourished in the \xe2\x80\x98church square\xe2\x80\x99 near the Oude Kerk until the Amsterdam\nmerchants built their own exchange building in 1611.<sup id="cite_ref-Kellenbenz_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kellenbenz-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Transactions had to be logged into the official accounts book in the East India house, indeed trading was highly sophisticated.<sup id="cite_ref-Stringham_21-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stringham-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Early trading in Amsterdam in the early 16th century (1560s\xe2\x80\x931611) largely occurred by the Nieuwe Brug bridge, near Amsterdam Harbor.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> Its proximity to the harbor and incoming mail made it a sensible location for traders to be the first to get the latest commercial news.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Shortly thereafter, the city of Amsterdam ordered the construction of an exchange in Dam Square. It opened in 1611 for business, and various sections of the building were marked for commodity trading and VOC securities.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> A bye-law on trade in the city dictated that trade could only take place in the exchange on weekdays from 11 a.m. to noon.<sup id="cite_ref-L.O._Petram._FGw_2011._p.30_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-L.O._Petram._FGw_2011._p.30-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> While only a short amount of time for trading inside the building, the window created a flurry of investors that in turn made it easier for buyers to find sellers and vice versa. Thus, the building of the stock exchange led to a vast expansion of liquidity in the marketplace. In addition, trading was continued in other buildings, outside of the trading hours of the exchange, such as the trading clubs, and was not prohibited in hours outside of those outlined in the bye-law.<sup id="cite_ref-L.O._Petram._FGw_2011._p.30_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-L.O._Petram._FGw_2011._p.30-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The location of exchange relative to the East India house was also strategic. Its proximity gave investors the luxury of walking a short distance to both register the transaction in the official books of the VOC, and complete the money transfer in the nearby Exchange Bank, also in Dam square.<sup id="cite_ref-L.O._Petram._FGw_2011._p.30_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-L.O._Petram._FGw_2011._p.30-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Brussels_.281801.E2.80.932000.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Brussels_(1801\xe2\x80\x932000)">Brussels (1801\xe2\x80\x932000)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euronext&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Brussels (1801\xe2\x80\x932000)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:La_Bourse_Bruxelles_1873.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/La_Bourse_Bruxelles_1873.jpg/220px-La_Bourse_Bruxelles_1873.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/La_Bourse_Bruxelles_1873.jpg/330px-La_Bourse_Bruxelles_1873.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/La_Bourse_Bruxelles_1873.jpg/440px-La_Bourse_Bruxelles_1873.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="443" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:La_Bourse_Bruxelles_1873.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Brussels Stock Exchange\'s building in 1873, shortly after its completion</div></div></div>\n<p>The Brussels Stock Exchange (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Bourse de Bruxelles</i>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>: <i lang="nl">Beurs van Brussel</i>) was founded in 1801 by decree of <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a>. As part of the <a href="/wiki/Covering_of_the_Senne" title="Covering of the Senne">covering of the river Senne</a> for health and aesthetic reasons in the 1860s and 1870s, a massive programme of beautification of the city centre was undertaken. Architect <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9on-Pierre_Suys" class="mw-redirect" title="L\xc3\xa9on-Pierre Suys">L\xc3\xa9on-Pierre Suys</a>, as part of his proposal for covering of the Senne, designed a building to become the centre of the rapidly expanding business sector. It was to be located on the former butter market, (itself situated on the ruins of the former <i>Recollets</i> <a href="/wiki/Franciscan" class="mw-redirect" title="Franciscan">Franciscan</a> convent) on the newly created <a href="/wiki/Boulevard_Anspach" title="Boulevard Anspach">Anspach Boulevard</a> (then called \'Central Boulevard\'). The building was erected from 1868 to 1873, and housed the Brussels Stock Exchange until 1996. The Bourse is due to become a beer museum and will open to the public in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The building does not have a distinct name, though it is usually called simply the <i lang="fr" title="French-language text">Bourse</i>/<i lang="nl" title="Dutch-language text">Beurs</i>. It is located on <a href="/wiki/Boulevard_Anspach" title="Boulevard Anspach">Boulevard Anspach</a>, and is the namesake of the <i><a href="/wiki/Place_de_la_Bourse_(Brussels)" class="mw-redirect" title="Place de la Bourse (Brussels)">Place de la Bourse/Beursplein</a></i>, which is, after the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Place" title="Grand Place">Grand Place</a>, the second most important square in Brussels. The building combines elements of the <a href="/wiki/Neo-Renaissance" class="mw-redirect" title="Neo-Renaissance">Neo-Renaissance</a> and <a href="/wiki/Second_Empire_(architecture)" class="mw-redirect" title="Second Empire (architecture)">Second Empire</a> architectural styles. It has an abundance of ornaments and sculptures, created by famous artists, including the brothers Jacques and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Jaquet" title="Joseph Jaquet">Joseph Jacquet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guillaume_de_Groot" title="Guillaume de Groot">Guillaume de Groot</a>, French sculptor <a href="/wiki/Albert-Ernest_Carrier-Belleuse" title="Albert-Ernest Carrier-Belleuse">Albert-Ernest Carrier-Belleuse</a> and his then-assistant <a href="/wiki/Auguste_Rodin" title="Auguste Rodin">Auguste Rodin</a>.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Paris_.281724.E2.80.932000.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Paris_(1724\xe2\x80\x932000)">Paris (1724\xe2\x80\x932000)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euronext&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Paris (1724\xe2\x80\x932000)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The Paris Stock Exchange (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Bourse de Paris</i>) was located in <i>Palais Brongniart</i> in the Place de la Bourse, in the <a href="/wiki/2nd_arrondissement_of_Paris" title="2nd arrondissement of Paris">II arrondissement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>. Historically, stock trading took place at several spots in Paris, including rue Quincampoix, rue Vivienne (near the <a href="/wiki/Palais_Royal" class="mw-redirect" title="Palais Royal">Palais Royal</a>), and the back of the <i><a href="/wiki/Op%C3%A9ra_Garnier" class="mw-redirect" title="Op\xc3\xa9ra Garnier">Op\xc3\xa9ra Garnier</a></i> (the Paris opera house).\n</p><p>\nIn the early 19th century, the Paris Bourse\'s activities found a stable location at the <i>Palais Brongniart</i>, or <i>Palais de la Bourse</i>, built to the designs of architect <a href="/wiki/Alexandre-Th%C3%A9odore_Brongniart" title="Alexandre-Th\xc3\xa9odore Brongniart">Alexandre-Th\xc3\xa9odore Brongniart</a> from 1808 to 1813 and completed by <a href="/wiki/%C3%89loi_Labarre" title="\xc3\x89loi Labarre">\xc3\x89loi Labarre</a> from 1813 to 1826.<sup id="cite_ref-Ayers_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ayers-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup></p><div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tavik_Frantisek_Simon_Die_Pariser_B%C3%B6rse.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Tavik_Frantisek_Simon_Die_Pariser_B%C3%B6rse.jpg/220px-Tavik_Frantisek_Simon_Die_Pariser_B%C3%B6rse.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Tavik_Frantisek_Simon_Die_Pariser_B%C3%B6rse.jpg/330px-Tavik_Frantisek_Simon_Die_Pariser_B%C3%B6rse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Tavik_Frantisek_Simon_Die_Pariser_B%C3%B6rse.jpg/440px-Tavik_Frantisek_Simon_Die_Pariser_B%C3%B6rse.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1355" data-file-height="1077" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tavik_Frantisek_Simon_Die_Pariser_B%C3%B6rse.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>Palais Brongniart</i> in 1900</div></div></div><p>Brongniart had spontaneously submitted his project, which was a rectangular <a href="/wiki/Empire_style" title="Empire style">neoclassical</a> Roman temple with a giant <a href="/wiki/Corinthian_order" title="Corinthian order">Corinthian</a> <a href="/wiki/Colonnade" title="Colonnade">colonnade</a> enclosing a <a href="/wiki/Vault_(architecture)" title="Vault (architecture)">vaulted</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arcade_(architecture)" title="Arcade (architecture)">arcaded</a> central chamber. His designs were greatly admired by <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a> and won Brongniart a major public commission at the end of his career. Initially praised, the building was later attacked for academic dullness. The authorities had required Brongniart to modify his designs, and after Brongniart\'s death in 1813, Labarre altered them even further, greatly weakening Brongniart\'s original intentions.  From 1901 to 1905 Jean-Baptiste-Frederic Cavel designed the addition of two lateral wings, resulting in a cruciform plan with innumerable columns. According to the architectural historian Andrew Ayers, these alterations "did nothing to improve the reputation of this uninspiring monument."<sup id="cite_ref-Ayers_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ayers-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From the second half of the 19th century, official stock markets in Paris were operated by the <i>Compagnie des agents de change</i>, directed by the elected members of a <a href="/wiki/Stockbroker" title="Stockbroker">stockbrokers</a>\' syndical council. The number of dealers in each of the different trading areas of the Bourse was limited. There were around 60 <i>agents de change</i> (the official stockbrokers). An <i>agent de change</i> had to be a French citizen, be\nnominated by a former agent or his estate, and be approved by the Minister of Finance, and he was appointed by decree of the President of the Republic. Officially, the <i>agents de change</i> could not trade for their own account nor even be a counterpart to someone who wanted to buy or sell securities with their aid; they were strictly brokers, that is, intermediaries. In the financial literature, the Paris Bourse is hence referred to as order-driven market, as opposed to quote-driven markets or dealer markets, where price-setting is handled by a dealer or market-maker. In Paris, only <i>agents de change</i> could receive a <a href="/wiki/Commission_(remuneration)" title="Commission (remuneration)">commission</a>, at a rate fixed by law, for acting as an intermediary. However, parallel arrangements were usual in order to favor some clients\' quote<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (September 2009)">clarification needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>. The Commodities Exchange was housed in the same building until 1889, when it moved to the present <i><a href="/wiki/Bourse_de_commerce_(Paris)" title="Bourse de commerce (Paris)">Bourse de commerce</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\nMoreover, until about the middle of the 20th century, a parallel market known as <i>"La Coulisse"</i> was in operation.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Until the late 1980s, the market operated as an <a href="/wiki/Open_outcry" title="Open outcry">open outcry</a> exchange, with the <i>agents de change</i> meeting on the exchange floor of the Palais Brongniart. In 1986, the Paris Bourse started to implement an electronic trading system. This was known generically as <a href="/wiki/CATS_(trading_system)" title="CATS (trading system)">CATS</a> (Computer Assisted Trading System), but the Paris version was called CAC (<a href="/wiki/Cotation_Assist%C3%A9e_en_Continu" title="Cotation Assist\xc3\xa9e en Continu">Cotation Assist\xc3\xa9e en Continu</a>). By 1989, quotations were fully automated. The Palais Brongniart hosted the French financial derivatives exchanges <a href="/wiki/MATIF" title="MATIF">MATIF</a> and <a href="/wiki/MONEP" class="mw-redirect" title="MONEP">MONEP</a>, until they were fully automated in 1998.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Lisbon_.281769.E2.80.932002.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Lisbon_(1769\xe2\x80\x932002)">Lisbon (1769\xe2\x80\x932002)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euronext&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Lisbon (1769\xe2\x80\x932002)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Porto_July_2014-31a.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Porto_July_2014-31a.jpg/220px-Porto_July_2014-31a.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Porto_July_2014-31a.jpg/330px-Porto_July_2014-31a.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8b/Porto_July_2014-31a.jpg/440px-Porto_July_2014-31a.jpg 2x" data-file-width="7158" data-file-height="4702" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Porto_July_2014-31a.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Pal%C3%A1cio_da_Bolsa" title="Pal\xc3\xa1cio da Bolsa">Stock Exchange Palace</a> in <a href="/wiki/Porto" title="Porto">Porto</a>, Portugal</div></div></div>\n<p>The predecessor of the Lisbon Stock Exchange (<a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>: <i lang="pt">Bolsa de Valores de Lisboa</i>) was created in 1769 as the <i>Assembleia dos Homens de Neg\xc3\xb3cio</i> (Assembly of Businessmen) in the <a href="/wiki/Pra%C3%A7a_do_Com%C3%A9rcio" title="Pra\xc3\xa7a do Com\xc3\xa9rcio">Commerce Square</a>, in downtown Lisbon. In 1891, the <i>Bolsa de Valores do Porto</i> (Oporto Stock Exchange) in <a href="/wiki/Oporto" class="mw-redirect" title="Oporto">Oporto</a> was founded.\n</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/Carnation_Revolution" title="Carnation Revolution">military coup</a> on April 25, 1974, both the Lisbon and Porto stock exchanges were closed by the revolutionary <i><a href="/wiki/National_Salvation_Junta" title="National Salvation Junta">National Salvation Junta</a></i> (they would be reopened a couple of years later).<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>At the end of 2001, 65 companies were listed on BVLP-regulated markets, representing a <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">market capitalization</a> of <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">Euro</a> 96.1 billion. From January to December 2001, a total of 4.7 million <a href="/wiki/Futures_contract" title="Futures contract">futures</a> and <a href="/wiki/Option_(finance)" title="Option (finance)">options</a> contracts were traded on the BVLP market.\n</p><p>The Euronext Lisbon was formed in 2002 when the shares of Bolsa de Valores de Lisboa e Porto (BVLP) were acquired by Euronext and the exchange was merged into the pan-European exchange. BVLP, the Portuguese exchange, was formed in the 1990s restructuring of the Lisbon Stock Exchange association and the Porto Derivatives Exchange Association.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Dublin_.281799.E2.80.932018.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Dublin_(1799\xe2\x80\x932018)">Dublin (1799\xe2\x80\x932018)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euronext&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Dublin (1799\xe2\x80\x932018)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:DUBLIN(1837)_p083_THE_ROYAL_EXCHANGE.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/DUBLIN%281837%29_p083_THE_ROYAL_EXCHANGE.jpg/220px-DUBLIN%281837%29_p083_THE_ROYAL_EXCHANGE.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/DUBLIN%281837%29_p083_THE_ROYAL_EXCHANGE.jpg/330px-DUBLIN%281837%29_p083_THE_ROYAL_EXCHANGE.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/DUBLIN%281837%29_p083_THE_ROYAL_EXCHANGE.jpg/440px-DUBLIN%281837%29_p083_THE_ROYAL_EXCHANGE.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1815" data-file-height="1125" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:DUBLIN(1837)_p083_THE_ROYAL_EXCHANGE.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Royal Exchange in 1837</div></div></div>\n<p>The Irish Stock Exchange (ISE; <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a>: <i lang="ga">Stocmhalart\xc3\xa1n na h\xc3\x89ireann</i>) was first recognised by legislation in 1799 when the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Ireland" title="Parliament of Ireland">Irish Parliament</a> passed the Stock Exchange (Dublin) Act.<a href="/wiki/Irish_Stock_Exchange#cite_note-3" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish Stock Exchange"><sup>[3]</sup></a> In different periods in its history, the ISE included a number of regional exchanges, including the <a href="/wiki/Cork_(city)" title="Cork (city)">Cork</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dublin" title="Dublin">Dublin</a> exchanges. The first woman to be admitted to a stock exchange was, <a href="/wiki/Oonah_Keogh" title="Oonah Keogh">Oonah Keogh</a> to the Dublin Stock Exchange in 1925. In 1973, the Irish exchange merged with British and other Irish stock exchanges becoming part of the International Stock Exchange of Great Britain and Ireland (now called the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a>).\n</p><p>In 1995, it became independent again and in April 2014 it demutualised changing its corporate structure and becoming a plc which is owned by a number of stockbroking firms.\n</p><p>At the time of its demutualisation the country\'s main stockbrokers received shares in the \xe2\x82\xac56m-valued exchange and dividing up \xe2\x82\xac26m in excess cash. <a href="/wiki/Davy_Stockbrokers" class="mw-redirect" title="Davy Stockbrokers">Davy Stockbrokers</a> took the largest stake, at 37.5 per cent, followed by <a href="/wiki/Goodbody_Stockbrokers" title="Goodbody Stockbrokers">Goodbody Stockbrokers</a> with 26.2 per cent; <a href="/wiki/Investec" title="Investec">Investec</a> with 18 per cent; the then <a href="/wiki/NatWest_Group" title="NatWest Group">Royal Bank of Scotland Group</a> 6.3 per cent; <a href="/wiki/Cantor_Fitzgerald" title="Cantor Fitzgerald">Cantor Fizgerald</a> 6 per cent; and Campbell O\xe2\x80\x99Connor with 6 per cent.\n</p><p>In March 2018, Euronext completed the purchase of the ISE, and renamed the ISE as Euronext Dublin.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span id="Oslo_.281818.E2.80.932019.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Oslo_(1818\xe2\x80\x932019)">Oslo (1818\xe2\x80\x932019)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euronext&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Oslo (1818\xe2\x80\x932019)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Euronext_Oslo.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Euronext_Oslo.jpg/220px-Euronext_Oslo.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="187" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Euronext_Oslo.jpg/330px-Euronext_Oslo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Euronext_Oslo.jpg/440px-Euronext_Oslo.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3104" data-file-height="2639" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Euronext_Oslo.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Oslo Stock Exchange</div></div></div>\n<p>Oslo B\xc3\xb8rs was established by a law of September 18, 1818. Trading on Oslo B\xc3\xb8rs commenced on April 15, 1819.\nIn 1881 Oslo B\xc3\xb8rs became a stock exchange, which means securities were listed. The first listing of securities contained 16 bond series and 23 stocks, including the Norwegian central bank (Norges Bank).\nOslo B\xc3\xb8rs cooperates with London Stock Exchange on trading systems. The exchange has also a partnership with the stock exchanges in Singapore and Toronto (Canada) for a secondary listing of companies.\nThe stock exchange was privatized in 2001, and is, after the merger in 2007, 100% owned by Oslo B\xc3\xb8rs VPS Holding ASA.\n</p><p>The over 180-year-old stock exchange building has been the subject of many long debates about how the building should be managed and designed over the years. Several of Christiania\'s (the name of Oslo between 1624 and 1925) best known business men fought for years to get approved and funded the construction of a stock exchange in Christiania, the capital of Norway from 1814.\n</p><p>In 1823 a building committee was appointed to consider the various suggested drawings at the time. The committee chose the architect Christian H. Grosch\'s proposal. On July 14, 1826 the Ministry approved the final plans of drawings and budgets. In 1828 it was called Norway\'s first monumental building, completed on the site called Gr\xc3\xb8nningen, the first public park in Christiania.\n</p><p>Oslo B\xc3\xb8rs Holding <a href="/wiki/Allmennaksjeselskap" class="mw-redirect" title="Allmennaksjeselskap">ASA</a> was the <a href="/wiki/Holding_company" title="Holding company">holding company</a> that owned <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Stock_Exchange" title="Oslo Stock Exchange">Oslo Stock Exchange</a> of <a href="/wiki/Norway" title="Norway">Norway</a> from 2001 to 2008.\n</p><p>The company was created in 2001 when the Oslo Stock Exchange was converted from a <a href="/wiki/Stiftelse" class="mw-redirect" title="Stiftelse">self-owning institution</a> to a public limited company. The ownership of Oslo B\xc3\xb8rs Holding was spread out between a large number of owners, the largest being <a href="/wiki/DnB_NOR" class="mw-redirect" title="DnB NOR">DnB NOR</a> (18%). The Nordic stock exchange group <a href="/wiki/OMX" class="mw-redirect" title="OMX">OMX</a> held a 10% stake as well. The company was not publicly listed. In 2008 it merged with <b>V</b>erdi<b>p</b>apir<b>s</b>entralen ASA (VPS) to create the new holding company <a href="/wiki/Oslo_B%C3%B8rs_VPS_Holding" class="mw-redirect" title="Oslo B\xc3\xb8rs VPS Holding">Oslo B\xc3\xb8rs VPS Holding ASA</a>.\n</p><p>Oslo B\xc3\xb8rs Holding had two subsidiaries, <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Stock_Exchange" title="Oslo Stock Exchange">Oslo B\xc3\xb8rs ASA</a> that operates the stock exchange and Oslo B\xc3\xb8rs Informasjon AS that manages the information systems of the exchange.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2000.E2.80.932001:_Founding"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2000\xe2\x80\x932001:_Founding">2000\xe2\x80\x932001: Founding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euronext&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 2000\xe2\x80\x932001: Founding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="box-Recentism plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-style ambox-Recentism" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/40px-Edit-clear.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/60px-Edit-clear.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/f2/Edit-clear.svg/80px-Edit-clear.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="48" data-file-height="48" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article or section <b>appears to be <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Recentism" title="Wikipedia:Recentism">slanted towards recent events</a>.</b><span class="hide-when-compact"> Please try to keep recent events in historical perspective and add more content related to non-recent events.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">June 2019</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Original_Euronext_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0b/Original_Euronext_logo.svg/220px-Original_Euronext_logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="106" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0b/Original_Euronext_logo.svg/330px-Original_Euronext_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/0/0b/Original_Euronext_logo.svg/440px-Original_Euronext_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="908" data-file-height="439" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Original_Euronext_logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Logo used between 2000 and 2007</div></div></div>\n<p>Euronext was formed on 22 September 2000 following a merger of the <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Stock_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Stock Exchange">Amsterdam Stock Exchange</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-NYSE_Euronext_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYSE_Euronext-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>  <a href="/wiki/Brussels_Stock_Exchange" title="Brussels Stock Exchange">Brussels Stock Exchange</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Paris_Bourse" class="mw-redirect" title="Paris Bourse">Paris Bourse</a>, in order to take advantage of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>\'s (EU) <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">single currency</a> and harmonisation of <a href="/wiki/Financial_market" title="Financial market">financial markets</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-foundation1_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foundation1-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-foundation2_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foundation2-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-foundation3_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foundation3-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-foundation4_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foundation4-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2001.E2.80.932007:_First_round_of_European_acquisitions"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2001\xe2\x80\x932007:_First_round_of_European_acquisitions">2001\xe2\x80\x932007: First round of European acquisitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euronext&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: 2001\xe2\x80\x932007: First round of European acquisitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In December 2001, Euronext acquired the shares of the <a href="/wiki/London_International_Financial_Futures_and_Options_Exchange" title="London International Financial Futures and Options Exchange">London International Financial Futures and Options Exchange</a> (LIFFE), forming Euronext.LIFFE. In 2002 the group merged with the Portuguese stock exchange Bolsa de Valores de Lisboa e Porto (BVLP), renamed <a href="/wiki/Euronext_Lisbon" title="Euronext Lisbon">Euronext Lisbon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-foundation3_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-foundation3-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> In 2001, Euronext became a listed company itself after completing its initial public offering.<sup id="cite_ref-Grace_Pownall_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grace_Pownall-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2003, Euronext cash products were integrated onto a single platform (NSC).<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2004, Euronext derivatives products were integrated onto <i>LIFFE CONNECT</i>. \n</p><p>In 2005, Euronext introduced <a href="/wiki/Alternext" class="mw-redirect" title="Alternext">Alternext</a> as a market segment to help finance small and mid-class companies in the Eurozone.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2007.E2.80.932012:_Merger_with_the_New_York_Stock_Exchange"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2007\xe2\x80\x932012:_Merger_with_the_New_York_Stock_Exchange">2007\xe2\x80\x932012: Merger with the New York Stock Exchange</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euronext&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: 2007\xe2\x80\x932012: Merger with the New York Stock Exchange">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/NYSE_Euronext" title="NYSE Euronext">NYSE Euronext</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Logo_of_NYSE_Euronext_2007-2012.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Logo_of_NYSE_Euronext_2007-2012.svg/220px-Logo_of_NYSE_Euronext_2007-2012.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="51" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Logo_of_NYSE_Euronext_2007-2012.svg/330px-Logo_of_NYSE_Euronext_2007-2012.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Logo_of_NYSE_Euronext_2007-2012.svg/440px-Logo_of_NYSE_Euronext_2007-2012.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="69" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Logo_of_NYSE_Euronext_2007-2012.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Logo of <a href="/wiki/NYSE_Euronext" title="NYSE Euronext">NYSE Euronext</a> from 2007 to 2012, based on NYSE\'s previous logo</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NYSE_Euronext_2012.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/NYSE_Euronext_2012.svg/220px-NYSE_Euronext_2012.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="68" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/NYSE_Euronext_2012.svg/330px-NYSE_Euronext_2012.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/NYSE_Euronext_2012.svg/440px-NYSE_Euronext_2012.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="725" data-file-height="223" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NYSE_Euronext_2012.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Logo used by NYSE Euronext from 2012 to 2014, which apart from "NYSE" was kept by the spun-off Euronext. Designed by Interbrand, the logo depicts a pixelated globe.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Due to apparent moves by <a href="/wiki/NASDAQ" class="mw-redirect" title="NASDAQ">NASDAQ</a> to acquire the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange" title="London Stock Exchange">London Stock Exchange</a><sup id="cite_ref-wsj_20061212_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj_20061212-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> or Euronext itself,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> NYSE Group, owner of the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">New York Stock Exchange</a> (NYSE), offered \xe2\x82\xac8 billion (US$10.2b) in cash and shares for Euronext on 22 May 2006, outbidding a rival offer for the European Stock exchange operator from <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_B%C3%B6rse" title="Deutsche B\xc3\xb6rse">Deutsche B\xc3\xb6rse</a>, the German stock market.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> Contrary to statements that it would not raise its bid, on 23 May 2006, Deutsche B\xc3\xb6rse unveiled a merger bid for Euronext, valuing the pan-European exchange at \xe2\x82\xac8.6 billion (US$11b), \xe2\x82\xac600 million over NYSE Group\'s initial bid.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Despite this, NYSE Group and Euronext penned a merger agreement, subject to shareholder vote and regulatory approval. The initial regulatory response by <a href="/wiki/Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" class="mw-redirect" title="Securities and Exchange Commission">SEC</a> chief <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Cox" title="Christopher Cox">Christopher Cox</a> (who was coordinating heavily with European counterparts) was positive, with an expected approval by the end of 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-online.wsj.com_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-online.wsj.com-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Deutsche B\xc3\xb6rse dropped out of the bidding for Euronext on 15 November 2006, removing the last major hurdle for the NYSE Euronext transaction. A run-up of NYSE Group\'s stock price in late 2006 made the offering far more attractive to Euronext\'s shareholders.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\nOn 19 December 2006, Euronext shareholders approved the transaction with 98.2% of the vote. Only 1.8% voted in favour of the Deutsche B\xc3\xb6rse offer. <a href="/wiki/Jean-Fran%C3%A7ois_Th%C3%A9odore" title="Jean-Fran\xc3\xa7ois Th\xc3\xa9odore">Jean-Fran\xc3\xa7ois Th\xc3\xa9odore</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Chief_executive_officer" title="Chief executive officer">chief executive officer</a> of Euronext, stated that they expected the transaction to close within three or four months.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>\nSome of the regulatory agencies with jurisdiction over the merger had already given approval. NYSE Group shareholders gave their approval on 20 December 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>\nThe merger was completed on 4 April 2007, forming <a href="/wiki/NYSE_Euronext" title="NYSE Euronext">NYSE Euronext</a>.\n</p><p>The new firm, <a href="/wiki/NYSE_Euronext" title="NYSE Euronext">NYSE Euronext</a>, was headquartered in New York City, with European operations and its trading platform run out of Paris. Then-NYSE <a href="/wiki/Chief_Executive_Officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief Executive Officer">CEO</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Thain" title="John Thain">John Thain</a>, who was to head NYSE Euronext, intended to use the combination to form the world\'s first global stock market, with continuous trading of stocks and derivatives over a 21-hour time span.  In addition, the two exchanges hoped to add <a href="/wiki/Borsa_Italiana" class="mw-redirect" title="Borsa Italiana">Borsa Italiana</a> (the Milan stock exchange) into the grouping.\n</p><p>In 2008 and 2009 <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_B%C3%B6rse" title="Deutsche B\xc3\xb6rse">Deutsche B\xc3\xb6rse</a> made two unsuccessful attempts to merge with NYSE Euronext. Both attempts did not enter into advanced steps of merger.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, Deutsche B\xc3\xb6rse and NYSE Euronext confirmed that they were in advanced merger talks. Such a merger would create the largest exchange in history.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The deal was approved by shareholders of NYSE Euronext on July 7, 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-online.wsj.com_51-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-online.wsj.com-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> and Deutsche B\xc3\xb6rse on July 15, 2011<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> and won the antitrust approved by the US regulators on December 22, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> On February 1, 2012, the deal was blocked by European Commission on the grounds that the new company would have resulted in a quasi-monopoly in the area of European financial derivatives traded globally on exchanges.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Deutsche B\xc3\xb6rse unsuccessfully appealed this decision.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Fairless2015_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fairless2015-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2012, Euronext announced the creation of Euronext London to offer listing facilities in the UK. As such, Euronext received in June, 2014 Recognized Investment Exchange (RIE) status from Britain\'s Financial Conduct Authority.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2012.E2.80.932014:_Acquisition_by_Intercontinental_Exchange"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2012\xe2\x80\x932014:_Acquisition_by_Intercontinental_Exchange">2012\xe2\x80\x932014: Acquisition by Intercontinental Exchange</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euronext&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: 2012\xe2\x80\x932014: Acquisition by Intercontinental Exchange">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 20 December 2012, the boards of directors of both <a href="/wiki/Intercontinental_Exchange" title="Intercontinental Exchange">Intercontinental Exchange</a> (ICE) and the NYSE Euronext approved an $8 billion acquisition of NYSE Euronext. Under the terms shareholders of NYSE would receive either $33.12 in cash for each share or .2581 IntercontinentalExchange Inc. shares, or a combination of $11.27 in cash per share plus .1703 shares of stock.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> The acquisition is subject to regulator approval, though since the operations of ICE and NYSE have little in common\xe2\x80\x94ICE is largely devoted to trading commodities, as opposed to NYSE\'s business of trading stocks and securities\xe2\x80\x94the deal is not expected to be blocked.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> ICE said that after the deal closed it would sell the Euronext portion of the company, including stock exchanges in Amsterdam, Brussels, Lisbon and Paris.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>  The deal went through and Euronext is a sister division to NYSE and part of ICE. ICE CEO <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_C._Sprecher" class="mw-redirect" title="Jeffrey C. Sprecher">Jeffrey C. Sprecher</a> would continue in that position at the combined company, while NYSE CEO Duncan Niederauer would serve as president.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>  The future of the New York Stock Exchange\'s historic trading floor under ICE has not been announced.  ICE closed the high profile and historic trading floors of its other earlier acquisitions, the <a href="/wiki/International_Petroleum_Exchange" class="mw-redirect" title="International Petroleum Exchange">International Petroleum Exchange</a> and the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Board_of_Trade" title="New York Board of Trade">New York Board of Trade</a> in New York.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimes1_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimes1-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2012 <a href="/wiki/Intercontinental_Exchange" title="Intercontinental Exchange">Intercontinental Exchange</a> (ICE) announced plans to acquire NYSE Euronext, owner of Euronext, in an $8.2 billion takeover.\n<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 2013, Euronext established Enternext as a subsidiary to help small and medium-size enterprises (SMEs) listed on Euronext outline and apply a strategy most suited to support their growth.<sup id="cite_ref-Europeanequities.nyx_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Europeanequities.nyx-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The ICE\'s deal was approved by the shareholders of NYSE Euronext and Intercontinental Exchange on June 3, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>\nThe European Commission approved the acquisition on 24 June 2013\n<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> \nand on Aug. 15, 2013 the US regulator, SEC, granted approval of the acquisition.\n<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\nEuropean regulators and ministries of Finance of the participating countries approved the deal and on November 13, 2013 the acquisition was completed.<sup id="cite_ref-ice1_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ice1-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ice2_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ice2-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2014.E2.80.932017:_Re-emergence"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2014\xe2\x80\x932017:_Re-emergence">2014\xe2\x80\x932017: Re-emergence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euronext&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: 2014\xe2\x80\x932017: Re-emergence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright" style=""><div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px"><div class="thumbimage noresize" style="width:450px;">\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1017906329">@media all and (max-width:720px){body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .mw-graph{min-width:100%!important;max-width:100%;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:visible}}.mw-parser-output .mw-graph-img{width:inherit;height:inherit}</style><div class="mw-graph mw-graph-always mw-graph-nofallback" style="min-width:100px;min-height:100px" data-graph-id="ad20f57021dd5e117af8028aaaf6592e397b817d"></div></div><div class="thumbcaption">Shareholders as of 17 June 2019. The reference shareholders are the Belgian <a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9_f%C3%A9d%C3%A9rale_de_participations_et_d%27investissement" class="extiw" title="fr:Soci\xc3\xa9t\xc3\xa9 f\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9rale de participations et d&#39;investissement">Federal Holding and Investment Company</a> (4.50%), the French <a href="/wiki/Caisse_des_d%C3%A9p%C3%B4ts_et_consignations" title="Caisse des d\xc3\xa9p\xc3\xb4ts et consignations">Deposits and Consignments Fund</a> (8.00%), <a href="/wiki/BNP_Paribas_Fortis" title="BNP Paribas Fortis">BNP Paribas Fortis</a> (2.22%), <a href="/wiki/ABN_AMRO" title="ABN AMRO">ABN AMRO</a> (0.55%) and <a href="/wiki/Euroclear" title="Euroclear">Euroclear</a> (8.00%).<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Part of ICE\'s deal to acquire NYSE Euronext was a spin-off for Euronext, which was considered a positive element for European stakeholders.<sup id="cite_ref-ice1_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ice1-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> After a complex series of operations, this occurred on 20 June 2014, through an <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> (IPO).<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The former <a href="/wiki/London_International_Financial_Futures_and_Options_Exchange" title="London International Financial Futures and Options Exchange">Euronext.LIFFE</a> was retained by ICE and renamed <i>ICE Futures Europe</i>. In order to stabilise Euronext, a consortium of eleven investors decided to invest in the company as "reference shareholders". These investors owned 33.36% of Euronext\'s capital and have a 3 years lockup period: <a href="/wiki/Euroclear" title="Euroclear">Euroclear</a>, <a href="/wiki/BNP_Paribas" title="BNP Paribas">BNP Paribas</a>, <a href="/wiki/BNP_Paribas_Fortis" title="BNP Paribas Fortis">BNP Paribas Fortis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9_G%C3%A9n%C3%A9rale" title="Soci\xc3\xa9t\xc3\xa9 G\xc3\xa9n\xc3\xa9rale">Soci\xc3\xa9t\xc3\xa9 G\xc3\xa9n\xc3\xa9rale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Caisse_des_d%C3%A9p%C3%B4ts_et_consignations" title="Caisse des d\xc3\xa9p\xc3\xb4ts et consignations">Caisse des D\xc3\xa9p\xc3\xb4ts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bpifrance" title="Bpifrance">BPI France</a>, <a href="/wiki/ABN_AMRO" title="ABN AMRO">ABN Amro</a>, ASR, <a href="/wiki/Banco_Esp%C3%ADrito_Santo" title="Banco Esp\xc3\xadrito Santo">Banco Espirito Santo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Banco_BPI" class="mw-redirect" title="Banco BPI">Banco BPI</a> and Belgian holding public company <a href="/w/index.php?title=Belgian_Federal_Holding_and_Investment_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Belgian Federal Holding and Investment Company (page does not exist)">Belgian Federal Holding and Investment Company</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soci%C3%A9t%C3%A9_F%C3%A9d%C3%A9rale_de_Participations_et_d%27Investissement" class="extiw" title="fr:Soci\xc3\xa9t\xc3\xa9 F\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9rale de Participations et d&#39;Investissement">fr</a>&#93;</span> (SFPI/FPIM).<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> They have 3 board seats.\n</p><p>In June 2014, EnterNext launched two initiatives to boost SME equity research and support the technology sector. EnterNext partnered with Morningstar to increase equity research focusing on mid-size companies, especially in the telecommunications, media and technology (TMT) sector.\n</p><p>On 22 September 2014, Euronext announced a partnership with <a href="/wiki/Degiro" title="Degiro">DEGIRO</a><sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> regarding the distribution of retail services of Euronext. Upon publishing the third quarter results for 2014, the partnership was seen as a plan for Euronext to compete more effectively on the Dutch retail segment.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 2017, Alternext was renamed to Euronext Growth.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2017.E2.80.93present:_Second_round_of_European_acquisitions"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2017\xe2\x80\x93present:_Second_round_of_European_acquisitions">2017\xe2\x80\x93present: Second round of European acquisitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euronext&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: 2017\xe2\x80\x93present: Second round of European acquisitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 14 August 2017, Euronext announced the completion of its acquisition of FastMatch, a currency trading platform.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 27 March 2018, Euronext announced the completion of its acquisition of the Irish Stock Exchange.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 18 June 2019, Euronext announced the completion of its acquisition of the <a href="/wiki/Oslo_Stock_Exchange" title="Oslo Stock Exchange">Oslo Stock Exchange</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 5 December 2019, Euronext announced that it would acquire 66% of the European <a href="/wiki/Electric_power" title="Electric power">power</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_commodities_exchanges" title="List of commodities exchanges">exchange</a> <a href="/wiki/Nord_Pool" title="Nord Pool">Nord Pool</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nordpoolgroup.com_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nordpoolgroup.com-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The acquisition was completed on 15 January 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 23 April 2020, Euronext announced that it would acquire ca. 70% of the Danish Central Securities Depository, <a href="https://da.wikipedia.org/wiki/VP_Securities" class="extiw" title="da:VP Securities">VP Securities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> The acquisition was completed on 4 August 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 18 September 2020, the <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange_Group" title="London Stock Exchange Group">London Stock Exchange Group</a> (LSEG) entered into exclusive talks to sell the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Bourse" title="Italian Bourse">Italian Bourse</a> (formally 100% of <i>London Stock Exchange Group Holdings Italia S.p.A.</i>), situated in <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a>, to Euronext.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> As part of the deal, CDP Equity, 100% owned by <a href="/wiki/Cassa_Depositi_e_Prestiti" title="Cassa Depositi e Prestiti">Cassa Depositi e Prestiti</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Intesa_Sanpaolo" title="Intesa Sanpaolo">Intesa Sanpaolo</a> would become Euronext shareholders.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> LSEG is selling Italian Bourse as part of regulatory remedies to see through its $27 billion purchase of data provider <a href="/wiki/Refinitiv" title="Refinitiv">Refinitiv</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> A \xe2\x82\xac4.3 bn deal was announced on 9 October, albeit contingent on the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> formally stating in mid-December that it will only permit LSEG\'s acquisition of Refinitiv if the Italian Bourse is sold. \nOn April 29, 2021, Euronext closed a deal to purchase Borsa Italians from <a href="/wiki/London_Stock_Exchange_Group" title="London Stock Exchange Group">London Stock Exchange Group</a> (LSEG) to acquire <a href="/wiki/Italian_Bourse" title="Italian Bourse">Borsa Italiana Group</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Euronext&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bourse_of_Antwerp" title="Bourse of Antwerp">Bourse of Antwerp</a>, the world\'s first financial exchange</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_European_Union" title="Economy of the European Union">Economy of the European Union</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Euroclear" title="Euroclear">Euroclear</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_European_stock_exchanges" title="List of European stock exchanges">List of European stock exchanges</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_stock_exchanges" title="List of stock exchanges">List of stock exchanges</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span
